CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of spaceflight-related accidents and incidents</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Space_disasters&amp;redirect=no" title="Space disasters">Space disasters</a>)</span></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Death in space" redirects here. For death in specifically outer space conditions, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_exposure" title="Space exposure">Space exposure</a>.</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Challenger_explosion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2879" data-file-width="3555" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Challenger_explosion.jpg/220px-Challenger_explosion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Challenger_explosion.jpg/330px-Challenger_explosion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Challenger_explosion.jpg/440px-Challenger_explosion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Challenger_explosion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">Space Shuttle <i>Challenger</i></a> disintegrates 73 seconds after its 1986 launch resulting in the death of all seven crew members.</div></div></div>\n<p>This article lists verifiable <b>spaceflight-related accidents and incidents</b> resulting in fatality or near-fatality during flight or training for manned space missions, and testing, assembly, preparation or flight of manned and unmanned spacecraft. Not included are accidents or incidents associated with <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile" title="Intercontinental ballistic missile">intercontinental ballistic missile</a> (ICBM) tests, unmanned space flights not resulting in fatality or serious injury, or <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Rocket-powered_aircraft" title="Rocket-powered aircraft">rocket-powered aircraft</a> projects of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Also not included are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lost_cosmonauts" title="Lost cosmonauts">alleged unreported Soviet space accidents</a>, which are considered <a href="/wiki/Fringe_theory" title="Fringe theory">fringe theories</a> by a majority of historians.\n</p><p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there have been 18 astronaut and cosmonaut fatalities during spaceflight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarwood2005_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarwood2005-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMusgrave,_Larsen,_Tommaso2009143_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMusgrave,_Larsen,_Tommaso2009143-2">[2]</a></sup> Astronauts have also died while training for space missions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">Apollo 1</a> launch pad fire which killed an entire crew of three. There have also been some non-astronaut fatalities during spaceflight-related activities.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1801" data-file-width="2593" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg/220px-Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg/330px-Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg/440px-Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astronauts_Memorial_Plaque.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Astronauts Memorial Plaque at Cape Canaveral (2015)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fallen_Astronaut.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1306" data-file-width="1306" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Fallen_Astronaut.jpg/220px-Fallen_Astronaut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Fallen_Astronaut.jpg/330px-Fallen_Astronaut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Fallen_Astronaut.jpg/440px-Fallen_Astronaut.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fallen_Astronaut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Fallen_Astronaut" title="Fallen Astronaut">Fallen Astronaut</a></i> memorial on the Moon, includes most spaceflight-related fatalities up to 1971</div></div></div>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronaut_fatalities">Astronaut fatalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Astronaut fatalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dd><i>(In the statistics below, "astronaut" is applied to all space travellers to avoid the use of "astronaut/cosmonaut".)</i></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_spaceflight">During spaceflight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: During spaceflight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of  December&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, in-flight accidents have killed 18 astronauts, in four separate incidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMusgrave,_Larsen,_Tommaso2009143_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMusgrave,_Larsen,_Tommaso2009143-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>NASA astronauts who died on duty are memorialized at the <a href="/wiki/Space_Mirror_Memorial" title="Space Mirror Memorial">Space Mirror Memorial</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center#Visitor_Complex" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex</a> in <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island,_Florida" title="Merritt Island, Florida">Merritt Island, Florida</a>.  Cosmonauts who died on duty under the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> were generally honored by burial at the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin_Wall_Necropolis" title="Kremlin Wall Necropolis">Kremlin Wall Necropolis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. No Soviet or Russian cosmonauts have died during spaceflight since 1971.\n</p><p>There have been a total of five fatal in-flight accidents, three of them flew above the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n_line" title="K&#225;rm&#225;n line">K&#225;rm&#225;n line</a>, and one was intended to do so. In each case, the entire crew was killed.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="3" cellspacing="3" class="wikitable">\n<caption>Orbital spaceflight fatalities\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr bgcolor="#cccccc">\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Incident</th>\n<th>Mission</th>\n<th>Fatalities</th>\n<th>Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="nowrap">1967-04-24</span>\n</td>\n<td>Parachute failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_1" title="Soyuz 1">Soyuz 1</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Komarov" title="Vladimir Komarov">Vladimir Komarov</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The one-day mission was plagued by a series of mishaps with the new spacecraft type, culminating with its <a href="/wiki/Parachute" title="Parachute">parachute</a> not opening properly after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_reentry" title="Atmospheric reentry">atmospheric reentry</a>. Komarov was killed when the capsule hit the ground at high speed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Komarov_dead_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Komarov_dead-4">[4]</a></sup>\n<p>The Soyuz 1 crash site coordinates are <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;params=51.3615_N_59.5622_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">51&#176;21&#8242;41&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">59&#176;33&#8242;44&#8243;E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">51.3615&#176;N 59.5622&#176;E</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">51.3615; 59.5622</span></span></span></a></span>, 3 kilometers (1.9&#160;mi) west of Karabutak, Province of Orenburg in the Russian Federation, about 275 kilometers (171&#160;mi) east-southeast of Orenburg. In a small park on the side of the road is a memorial monument: a black column with a bust of Komarov at the top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="nowrap">1971-06-30</span>\n</td>\n<td>Decompression in space\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_11" title="Soyuz 11">Soyuz 11</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Georgy_Dobrovolsky" title="Georgy title="Vladislav Volkov">Vladislav Volkov</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The crew of <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_11" title="Soyuz 11">Soyuz 11</a> were killed after undocking from <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> <a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">Salyut 1</a> after a three-week stay. A cabin vent valve accidentally opened at service module separation. The recovery team found the crew dead. These three are the only human fatalities <i>in space</i> (above 100 kilometers (330,000&#160;ft)) thus far.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soyuz_11_crew_dead_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soyuz_11_crew_dead-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soyuz_11_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soyuz_11-9">[9]</a></sup>\n<p>The Soyuz 11 landing coordinates are <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;params=47.35663_N_70.12142_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">47&#176;21&#8242;24&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">70&#176;07&#8242;17&#8243;E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">47.35663&#176;N 70.12142&#176;E</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">47.35663; 70.12142</span></span></span></a></span>, 90 kilometers (56&#160;mi) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Karazhal" title="Karazhal">Karazhal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karagandy" title="Karagandy">Karagandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, and about 550 kilometers (340&#160;mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Baikonur" title="Baikonur">Baikonur</a>, in open flat country far from any populated area. In a small circular fenced area at the site is a memorial monument in the form of a three-sided metallic column. Near the top of the column on each side is the engraved image of the face of a crew member set into a stylized triangle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a title="Michael J. Smith (astronaut)">Michael J. Smith</a></span> <br/><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Dick_Scobee" title="Dick Scobee">Dick Scobee</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The Space Shuttle <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger"><i>Challenger</i></a> was destroyed 73 seconds after lift-off on <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">STS-51-L</a> at an altitude of 15 kilometers (49,000&#160;ft). The investigation found that cold weather conditions caused an <a href="/wiki/O-ring" title="O-ring">O-ring</a> seal to fail, allowing hot gases from the shuttle <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">solid rocket booster (SRB)</a> to impinge on the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">external propellant tank</a> and booster strut. The strut and aft end of the tank failed, allowing the top of the SRB to rotate into the top of the tank. <i>Challenger</i> was thrown sideways into the <a href="/wiki/Mach_number" title="Mach number">Mach</a> 1.8 windstream and broke up with the loss of all seven crew members. NASA investigators determined they may have survived the spacecraft disintegration, possibly unconscious from <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)" title="Hypoxia (medical)">hypoxia</a>; some tried to activate their emergency oxygen.  Any survivors of the breakup were killed, however, when the largely intact <a href="/wiki/Cockpit" title="Cockpit">cockpit</a> hit the water at 320&#160;km/h (200&#160;mph), about 32&#160;km (20&#160;miles) east of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">Cape Canaveral</a> at 28.64 degrees north, 80.28 degrees west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> About half of the vehicle\'s remains were never recovered, and fragments still wash ashore occasionally on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Brevard_County,_Florida" title="Brevard County, Florida">Brevard County, Florida</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="nowrap">2003-02-01</span>\n</td>\n<td>Vehicle disintegration on re-entry &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">Space Shuttle <i>Columbia</i> disaster</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">STS-107</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Rick_Husband" title="Rick Husband">Rick D. Ramon</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The Space Shuttle <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia"><i>Columbia</i></a> was lost as it returned from a two-week mission, <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">STS-107</a>. Damage to the shuttle\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space shuttle thermal protection system">thermal protection system (TPS)</a> led to structural failure of the shuttle\'s left wing and the spacecraft ultimately broke apart during reentry at an altitude of under 65&#160;km. Investigation revealed damage to the reinforced carbon-carbon leading edge wing panel resulted from the impact of a piece of foam insulation that broke away from the external tank during the launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n<p>The vehicle broke up over the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">southwestern United States</a> and fell in fragments over eastern <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and central <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>.\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Spaceflight fatalities below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karman_line" title="Karman line">Karman line</a>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Incident</th>\n<th>Mission</th>\n<th>Fatalities</th>\n<th>Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="nowrap">1967-11-15</span>\n</td>\n<td>Control failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/X-15_Flight_3-65-97" title="X-15 Flight 3-65-97">X-15 Flight 3-65-97</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Adams" title="Michael J. Adams">Michael J. Adams</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>During X-15 Flight 191, Adams\' seventh flight, the plane had an electrical problem followed by control problems at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apogee" title="Apogee">apogee</a> of its flight. The pilot may also have become disoriented. During reentry from a 266,000&#160;ft (50.4 mile, 81.1&#160;km) apogee, the X-15 yawed and went into a spin at Mach 5. The pilot recovered, but went into a Mach 4.7 inverted dive. Excessive loading led to structural breakup at about 65,000 feet (19.8&#160;km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Adams was posthumously awarded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronaut_Badge" title="Astronaut Badge">astronaut wings</a>, as his flight had passed an altitude of 50 miles (80.5&#160;km),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X-15_death_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-X-15_death-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_training_or_testing">During training or testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: During training or testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In addition to accidents during spaceflights, 13 astronauts, test pilots, and other personnel have been killed during training and test flights.\n</p>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="3" cellspacing="3" class="wikitable">\n<caption>Fatalities during training or testing for spaceflight\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr bgcolor="#cccccc">\n<th>Incident</th>\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Mission (program)</th>\n<th>Fatalities</th>\n<th>Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Fire in altitude chamber\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">23 March 1961</span>\n</td>\n<td>(Soviet Air Force Group 1)\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union"><img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Valentin_Bondarenko" title="Valentin Bondarenko">Valentin Bondarenko</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>First space-related fatality. During a 15-day endurance experiment in a low-pressure altitude chamber with at least 50% <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> atmosphere, <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">Vostok</a> cosmonaut trainee Bondarenko dropped an alcohol-soaked cloth onto an electric hotplate. He suffered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-degree_burns" title="Third-degree burns">third-degree burns</a> over most of his body and face, and died in a hospital 16 hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bondarenko\'s_Death_announced_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bondarenko\'s_Death_announced-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Training jet crash\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">31 October 1964</span>\n</td>\n<td>(<a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Group_3" title="NASA Astronaut Group 3">NASA Astronaut Group 3</a>)\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Freeman" title="Theodore Freeman">Theodore Freeman</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Before being selected for a Gemini crew, Freeman was flying a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northrop_T-38" title="Northrop T-38">T-38</a> jet trainer on landing approach to Ellington AFB near Houston, TX, when a <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">goose</a> smashed into the left side of the cockpit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canopy_(aircraft)" title="Canopy (aircraft)">canopy</a>. Shards of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plexiglas" title="Plexiglas">Plexiglas</a> entered the engine intake and caused both engines to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flame_out" title="Flame out">flame out</a>. Freeman <a href="/wiki/Ejection_seat" title="Ejection seat">ejected</a> too close to the ground for his parachute to open properly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1966_NASA_T-38_crash" title="1966 NASA T-38 crash">Training jet crash</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">28 February 1966</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gemini_9A" title="Gemini 9A">Gemini 9</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Elliot_See" title="Elliot See">Elliot See</a></span><br/><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bassett" title="Charles Bassett">Charles Bassett</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>See and Bassett attempted to land their T-38 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lambert_Field" title="Lambert Field">Lambert Field</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a> in bad weather, and crashed into the adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McDonnell_Aircraft" title="McDonnell Aircraft">McDonnell Aircraft</a> factory, where they were going for simulator training for their Gemini 9 flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Fire during spacecraft test\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">27 January 1967</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">Apollo 1</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" "Gus" Grissom</a></span> <br/><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" Chaffee">Roger B. Chaffee</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>An electrical fire in the cabin spread quickly in the pure oxygen atmosphere and claimed the lives of all three Apollo 1 crew members during a "plugs-out" test in preparation for their planned February 21 launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Training jet crash\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">5 October 1967</span>\n</td>\n<td>(<a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo</a>)\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Williams" title="Clifton Williams">Clifton C. Williams</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Williams, flying alone in a T-38 jet from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Kennedy" title="Cape Kennedy">Cape Kennedy</a>, Florida to <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas, crashed due to an aileron control mechanical failure, about 15 miles (24&#160;km) north of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tallahassee" title="Tallahassee">Tallahassee</a>, Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Williams ejected too low for the parachute to open properly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Williams had been selected as lunar module pilot on an Apollo crew with commander <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">Pete Conrad</a> and command module pilot <a href="/wiki/Richard_F._Gordon_Jr." title="Richard F. Gordon Jr.">Richard Gordon</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Training jet crash\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">8 December 1967</span>\n</td>\n<td>(<a href="/wiki/Manned_Orbiting_Laboratory" title="Manned Orbiting Laboratory">Manned Orbiting Laboratory</a>)\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Henry_Lawrence_Jr." title="Robert Henry Lawrence Jr.">Robert Henry Lawrence Jr.</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The first African-American astronaut, selected for the Air Force <a href="/wiki/Manned_Orbiting_Laboratory" title="Manned Orbiting Laboratory">Manned Orbiting Laboratory</a> program, was killed when his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-104_Starfighter" title="F-104 Starfighter">F-104 Starfighter</a> jet crashed at <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">Edwards Air Force Base</a>, California, while practicing a series of high speed, quick descent landings with Major Harvey Royer as pilot in command. Both crewmen ejected; Royer survived with injuries, but Lawrence, the instructor pilot, was found in his ejection seat, parachute not fully deployed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Drowned during water recovery training\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">11 July 1993</span>\n</td>\n<td>(Soviet Air Force Cosmonaut Training Group 11)\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia"><img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Vozovikov" title="Sergei Vozovikov">Sergei Vozovikov</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Sergei Yuriyevich Vozovikov was a member of the Soviet Air Force Cosmonaut Training Group 11. His Cosmonaut training was from 1 October 1991 to 6 March 1992. He drowned 11 July 1993 during water recovery training in the Black Sea, near <a href="/wiki/Anapa" title="Anapa">Anapa</a>, Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disasters_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disasters-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/VSS_Enterprise_crash" title="VSS Enterprise crash">Spaceplane crash during test flight</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">31 October 2014</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/VSS_Enterprise" title="VSS Enterprise">VSS Enterprise</a> PF04\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Alsbury" title="Michael Alsbury">Michael Alsbury</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Michael_Alsbury" title="Michael Alsbury">Michael Alsbury</a> was killed and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Siebold" title="Peter Siebold">Peter Siebold</a> was seriously injured when <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipTwo" title="SpaceShipTwo">SpaceShipTwo</a> <a href="/wiki/VSS_Enterprise" title="VSS Enterprise">VSS <i>Enterprise</i></a> disintegrated during a powered atmospheric test flight over California due to premature deployment of the <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_entry#Feathered_reentry" title="Atmospheric entry">feathering system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-fatal_incidents_during_spaceflight">Non-fatal incidents during spaceflight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Non-fatal incidents during spaceflight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Apart from actual disasters, a number of missions resulted in some very near misses and also some training accidents that nearly resulted in deaths.\n</p>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="3" cellspacing="3" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr bgcolor="#cccccc">\n<th>Incident</th>\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Mission</th>\n<th>Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Separation failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">12 April 1961</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>After retrofire, the Vostok service module unexpectedly remained attached to the reentry module by a bundle of wires. The two halves of the craft were supposed to separate ten seconds after retrofire. But they did not separate until 10 minutes after retrofire, when the wire bundle finally burned through. The spacecraft went into wild gyrations at the beginning of reentry, before the wires burned through and the reentry module settled into the proper reentry attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vostok_1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vostok_1-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Landing capsule sank in water\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">21 July 1961</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mercury-Redstone_4" title="Mercury-Redstone 4">Mercury-Redstone 4</a>\n</td>\n<td>After splashdown in the Atlantic, the hatch malfunctioned and blew, filling the capsule with water and almost drowning <a href="/wiki/Gus_Grissom" title="Gus Grissom">Gus Grissom</a>, who managed to escape before it sank. Grissom then had to deal with a spacesuit that was rapidly filling with water, but managed to get into the helicopter\'s retrieval collar and was lifted to safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liberty_Bell_7_Sinks_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liberty_Bell_7_Sinks-33">[33]</a></sup> The spacecraft was recovered in 1999, having settled 300&#160;nmi (560&#160;km; 350&#160;mi) southeast of Cape Canaveral in 15,000&#160;ft (4,600&#160;m) of seawater. An unexploded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SOFAR_bomb" title="SOFAR bomb">SOFAR bomb</a>, designed for sound fixing and ranging in case the craft sank, had failed and had to be dealt with when it was recovered from the ocean floor in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOFAR_bomb_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOFAR_bomb-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Spacesuit or airlock design fault\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">18 March 1965</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">Voskhod 2</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The mission featured the world\'s first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">spacewalk</a>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Leonov" title="Alexei Leonov">Alexei Leonov</a>. After his twelve minutes outside, Leonov\'s spacesuit inflated in the vacuum to the point where he could not reenter the airlock. He opened a valve to allow some of the suit\'s pressure to bleed off, and was barely able to get back inside the capsule after suffering side effects of <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">the bends</a>. Because the spacecraft was so cramped, the crew could not keep to their reentry schedule and landed 386&#160;km off course in deep forest. They spent a night sheltering in the capsule from the cold, and a second night in a temporary hut built by rescuers before skiing with them to a clearing where a helicopter flew them to <a href="/wiki/Perm" title="Perm">Perm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Engine shutdown at launch\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">12 December 1965</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Gemini_6A" title="Gemini 6A">Gemini 6A</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The first on-pad shutdown in the US Manned Program.  <a href="/wiki/Gemini_7" title="Gemini 7">Gemini 7</a> orbiting 185 miles (298&#160;km) directly over Missile Row witnessed the event and reported they could clearly see the momentary exhaust plume before shutdown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gemini6A_abort_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gemini6A_abort-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Equipment failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">17 March 1966</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Gemini_8" title="Gemini 8">Gemini 8</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>A maneuvering thruster refused to shut down and put their capsule into an uncontrolled spin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gemini_8_close_call_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gemini_8_close_call-38">[38]</a></sup> After the Gemini spun up to one revolution per second, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">Neil Armstrong</a> regained control by switching from the main attitude control system to the reentry system.  Mission rules required a landing as soon as possible once the reentry thrusters were used, causing an early end to the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nssdc1966_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-nssdc1966-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Separation failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">18 January 1969</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_5" title="Soyuz 5">Soyuz 5</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Harrowing reentry and landing when the capsule\'s service module initially refused to separate, causing the spacecraft to begin reentry faced the wrong way. The service module broke away before the capsule would have been destroyed, and so it made a rough but survivable landing far off course in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ural_mountains" title="Ural mountains">Ural mountains</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Struck twice by lightning during launch\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">14 November 1969</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">Apollo 12</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Two lightning strikes during launch. The first strike, at 36 seconds after liftoff, knocked the three fuel cells offline and the craft switched to battery power automatically. The second strike, at 52 seconds after liftoff, knocked the onboard guidance platform offline. Four temperature sensors on the outside of the Lunar Module were burnt out and four measuring devices in the reaction control system failed temporarily. Fuel cell power was restored about four minutes later. The astronauts spent additional time in Earth orbit to make sure the spacecraft was functional before firing their S-IVB third stage engine and departing for the Moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Struck by camera during splashdown\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">24 November 1969</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">Apollo 12</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Astronaut Alan Bean was struck above the right eyebrow by a 16mm movie camera when the spacecraft <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Splashdown_(spacecraft_landing)" title="Splashdown (spacecraft landing)">splashed down</a> in the ocean. The camera broke free from its storage place. Bean suffered a <a href="/wiki/Concussion" title="Concussion">concussion</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and a 1.25&#160;cm cut above the eyebrow that required stitches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Premature engine shutdown\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">11 April 1970</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">Apollo 13</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>During launch, the Saturn V second stage experienced a premature shutdown on one of its five engines. The center engine shut down two minutes early. The remaining engines on the second and third stages were burned a total of 34 seconds longer to compensate. It was later determined that the shutdown was caused by <a href="/wiki/Pogo_oscillation" title="Pogo oscillation">pogo oscillation</a> of the engine. <a href="/wiki/Parking_orbit" title="Parking orbit">Parking orbit</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Translunar_injection" title="Translunar injection">translunar injection</a> were successfully achieved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Equipment failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">13 April 1970</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">Apollo 13</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The crew came home safely after a violent rupture of a liquid oxygen tank<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> deprived the Service Module of its ability to produce electrical power, crippling their spacecraft en route to the moon. They survived the loss of use of their command ship by relying on the Lunar Module as a "life boat" to provide life support and power for the trip home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>One of three main parachutes failed\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">7 August 1971</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">Apollo 15</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>During descent, the three main parachutes opened successfully. However, when the remaining reaction control system fuel was jettisoned, one parachute was damaged by the discarded fuel causing it to collapse. Spacecraft and  crew still <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Splashdown_(spacecraft_landing)" title="Splashdown (spacecraft landing)">splashed down</a> safely, at a slightly higher than normal velocity, on the two remaining main parachutes. This also interrupted the craft\'s attitude, causing the vehicle to accelerate towards the Earth and triggering an emergency reentry sequence. Due to the downward acceleration, the crew experienced an acceleration of 21.3 <i>g</i> rather than the nominal 15 <i>g</i> for an abort. Upon landing, the vehicle rolled down a hill and stopped just short of a high cliff. The crew members suffered from burning sensations of their eyes, faces, noses, throats and lungs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Patten_Stafford" title="Thomas Patten Stafford">Thomas Stafford</a> quickly broke out emergency oxygen masks and put one on Brand and gave one to <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">Deke Slayton</a>. The crew were exposed to the toxic fumes from 24,000&#160;ft (7.3&#160;km) down to landing. About an hour after landing the crew developed chemical-induced pneumonia and their lungs had <a href="/wiki/Edema" title="Edema">edema</a>. They experienced shortness of breath and were hospitalized in Hawaii. The crew spent five days in the hospital, followed by a week of observation in semi-isolation. By July 30, their chest X-rays appeared to return to normal except for Slayton; he was diagnosed with a benign lesion, unrelated to the gas exposure, which was later removed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Landing capsule sank in water\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">16 October 1976</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_23" title="Soyuz 23">Soyuz 23</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>The capsule broke through the surface of a frozen lake and was dragged underwater by its parachute. Some of the aft structures on <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia"><i>Columbia</i></a> reached their design limits (2.0 psi) from the overpressure. An improved water spray shock wave damping system had to be installed on the launch pad prior to launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Fire in launch vehicle\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">26 September 1983</span>\n</td>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_7K-ST_No.16L" title="Soyuz 7K-ST No.16L">Soyuz T-10-1</a>\n</td>\n<td>A fuel spillage before the planned liftoff caused the vehicle to be engulfed in flames. About 15 minutes after landing, hydrazine fuel trapped in the APU control valves exploded, destroying the valves in both APUs. The fire also damaged nearby wiring. The fire stopped when the supply of leaked fuel was exhausted. All of this was discovered the next day when technicians removed an access panel and discovered the area blackened and scorched. It is believed that hydrazine leaked in orbit and froze, stopping the leak. After returning, the leak restarted and ignited when combined with oxygen from the atmosphere. There were no injuries during the incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Space Shuttle in-flight engine failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">29 July 1985</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"> <a href="/wiki/STS-51-F" title="STS-51-F">STS-51-F</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>Five minutes, 45 seconds into ascent, one of three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Main_Engine" title="Space Shuttle Main Engine">main engines</a> aboard <i>Challenger</i> shut down prematurely due to a spurious high temperature reading. At about the same time, a second main engine almost shut down from a similar problem, but this was observed and inhibited by a fast acting <a href="/wiki/Flight_controller" title="Flight controller">flight controller</a>. The failed SSME resulted in an <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_abort_modes#Abort_to_Orbit_(ATO)" title="Space Shuttle abort modes">Abort To Orbit (ATO)</a> trajectory, whereby the shuttle achieves a lower than planned orbital altitude. Had the second engine failed within about 20 seconds of the first, a <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_abort_modes#Transoceanic_abort_landing" title="Space Shuttle abort modes">Transoceanic Abort Landing (TAL)</a> abort might have been necessary. No bailout option existed until after mission STS-51-L, the <i>Challenger</i> disaster.  But even with that option, a bailout (a "contingency abort") would never be considered when an "intact abort" option exists, and after five minutes of normal flight it would always exist unless a serious flight control failure or some other major problem beyond engine shutdown occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDumoulin2000_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDumoulin2000-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shuttle_Close_Call_1985_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shuttle_Close_Call_1985-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Sensor failure\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">6 September 1988</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Mir_EP-3" title="Mir EP-3">Mir EP-3</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>At the end of the mission, Soviet cosmonaut <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lyakhov" title="Vladimir Lyakhov">Vladimir Lyakhov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghan</a> cosmonaut <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Ahad_Mohmand" title="Abdul Ahad Mohmand">Abdul Ahad Mohmand</a> undocked from <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a> in the spacecraft <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-5" title="Soyuz TM-5">Soyuz TM-5</a>. During descent they suffered a computer software problem combined with a sensor problem. The deorbit engine on the TM-5 spacecraft which was to propel them into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_reentry" title="Atmospheric reentry">atmospheric reentry</a>, did not behave as expected. During an attempted burn, the computer shut off the engines prematurely, believing the spacecraft was out of alignment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174-60">[60]</a></sup> Lyakhov determined that they were not, in fact, out of alignment, and asserted that the problem was caused by conflicting signals picked up by the alignment sensors caused by solar glare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174-60">[60]</a></sup> With the problem apparently solved, two orbits later he restarted to deorbit engines. But the engines shut off again. The flight director decided that they would have to remain in orbit an extra day (a full revolution of the Earth), so they could determine what the problem was. During this time it was realised that during the second attempted engine burn, the computer had tried to execute the program which was used to dock with Mir several months earlier during <a href="/wiki/Mir_EP-2" title="Mir EP-2">EP-2</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarland2005173&#8211;174-60">[60]</a></sup> After reprogramming the computer, the next attempt was successful, and the crew safely landed on 7 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFurniss,_Shayler,_Shayler2007355_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFurniss,_Shayler,_Shayler2007355-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Thermal tile damage\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">6 December 1988</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/STS-27" title="STS-27">STS-27</a></span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis"><i>Atlantis</i></a>\' Thermal Protection System tiles sustained unusually severe damage during this flight. Ablative insulating material from the right-hand solid rocket booster nose cap had hit the orbiter about 85 seconds into the flight, as seen in footage of the ascent. The crew made an inspection of the shuttle\'s impacted starboard side using the shuttle\'s <a href="/wiki/Canadarm" title="Canadarm">Canadarm</a> robot arm, but the limited resolution and range of the cameras made it impossible to determine the full extent of the tile damage. Following reentry, more than 700 tiles were found to be damaged including one that was missing entirely. STS-27 was the most heavily damaged shuttle to return to earth safely.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Spacesuit puncture\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">8 April 1991</span>\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/STS-37" title="STS-37">STS-37</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>During an <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_activity" title="Extravehicular activity">extravehicular activity</a>, a small rod (palm bar) in a glove of EV2 astronaut <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay_Apt" title="Jay Apt">Jay Apt</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extravehicular_mobility_unit" title="Extravehicular mobility unit">extravehicular mobility unit</a> punctured the suit. The engines automatically switched to their backup controllers. Had a further short shut down two engines, <i>Columbia</i> would have ditched in the ocean, although the crew could have possibly bailed out. A defective quick-disconnect valve allowed 5% of the ammonia cooling supply to escape into space. The escaping ammonia froze on the spacesuit of astronaut Curbeam as he struggled to close the valve. His helmet and suit were coated in ammonia crystals an inch thick. Mission Control instructed Curbeam to remain outside for an entire orbit to allow the Sun to evaporate the frozen ammonia from his spacesuit. When they returned to the airlock, the astronauts pressurized, vented and then repressurized the air lock to purge any remaining toxic ammonia. After they removed their spacesuits, the crew wore oxygen masks for another 20 minutes to allow life-support systems in the airlock to further filter the air. No injuries resulted from the incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Ballistic reentry, injured shoulder\n</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">3 May 2003</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-1" title="Soyuz TMA-1">Soyuz TMA-1</a>\n</td>\n<td>The capsule had a malfunction during its return to Earth from the ISS <a href="/wiki/Expedition_6" title="Expedition 6">Expedition 6</a> mission and performed a ballistic reentry.
